## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and possibly time t (external driving). The equation of motion combines nonlinear restoring forces, nonlinear damping, and potential periodic forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator (damped, driven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity-dependent friction)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonic potential)
- Pendulum-like (small angle expansion): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (Taylor expansion of sin(x))
- Sinusoidal restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (pendulum-type nonlinearity)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) + c2 * v (time-modulated stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping with restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 + c2 * v (position-dependent damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Coulomb + viscous friction: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * (v**2)**(-0.5) (mixed friction model, effectively sign function)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent frequency)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) â†’ symmetric potential wells preserving oscillatory symmetry
- Position-velocity coupling terms (v*x^2) â†’ amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of Van der Pol-type self-excited oscillations
- Sinusoidal time dependence in acceleration â†’ external periodic driving force; look for cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) terms
- Cubic position terms with opposite sign to linear term â†’ Duffing-type hardening/softening spring behavior
- Velocity terms with odd powers (v, v**3) â†’ dissipative forces; even powers of v multiplied by v â†’ nonlinear drag
- Absence of explicit time dependence â†’ autonomous system; presence suggests driven/parametric excitation
- Product x*v terms â†’ energy-dependent coupling, often arising in self-sustained oscillators
- sin(c*x) restoring force â†’ large-amplitude pendulum dynamics beyond small-angle approximation
